<name>Desmond Forden<//name>< Review>
With so many Mexican options in San Diego in general and Mira Mesa as well, La Mexican Fiesta always seemed to slip under the radar. Perhaps it's because this isn't one of your 24 hr places and my cravings for Mexican food are loosely correlated with late night drinking. It's not my fault. It's a disease ok?!

Anyway, I finally stopped by during open hours (barely) and was able to tryout some Carne Asada fries - the go to standard metric of San Diego Mexican eateries. Since they about to close I took it too go. The dine in area is smaller but festive. The food itself was pretty good. A creamier guac sauce was used instead of a traditional guacamole but I'm not one that actually minds that. There wasn't as much food as other places will give you but I was pretty satisfied overall. I'll be trying to come more often since it is actually closer than other places but it just depends on when the cravings hit!</Review>

Drinks/Crepes: The crepe itself is very good! We got the green tea crepes. Nice and fluffy but also crispy at the same time! Oh, did I mention all of their ingredients are organic?! We also go the sparkling lemonade! That was super refreshing.

<Rate>5<//Rate><text>This is my favorite japanese style crepe place. I have been coming here for years and it never disappoints. First time was in 2011.

Toppings and ingredients are always fresh. The creeper batter is always amazing, lots of flavor and the right amount of chewiness to lightness.

Prices can get high if you build your own crepe, but the location is in Beverly Hills..

I always get the Nutty Banana with earl grey crepe but they no longer have the earl grey. A little disappointing but they have other great choices.

Staff is friendly, and the place is quite small. So, if you catch it at a busy time, it's tough to move around.<//text>< Pics>

< Text>
I had a Harajuku Crepe in Japan and this place in Beverly Hills tasted better!! :) I'm impressed! :D

This is a cute little cafe in Beverly Hills. There are about 2 small tables and a couch for seating. The guy who makes the crepes is Japanese and is really nice!

If you're here, you gotta try a crepe. You can also order boba or tea too. How it works is that you get to customize your crepe by which type of crepe you want, fruits, toppings, fillings, and/or ice cream. And with each thing you choose, there's a cost.

What I got:
-Earl grey crepe $3
-Strawberries $1
-Whipped cream $0.50
-Nutella $0.50
-Green tea ice cream $0.50

Total: $6 (Totally worth it!!)

The crepe was thin and perfectly cooked! Everything was well-portioned and wasn't too sweet.

Only downside is the parking. You gotta try to find a meter or park in one of the public lots/garages.

Overall, I am a fan and will definitely be back! A great place for dessert!<//Text>

This place is located in the  heart of Beverly Hills,  right off of rodeo drive.  It's kind of a hole in the wall,  which is weird because of its location.

The menu is create your own, with each topping ranging from $0.50 - $1.00. I came here for the the early Grey crepe, which sets it apart from other crepe places.  I topped it off with red beans,  big mochi balls,  and black sesame ice cream.  First bite,  amazing! You can actually taste the Earl Grey flavor.  Their ice cream and mochi balls were delicious.  If you're in the  area,  definitely stop by and support this small business.</text>

< Review>
This place is so damn good!

I've been wanting to try this place for the longest! We had dinner on the Westside and decided to save room to try Harajuku Crepe for dessert.

We shared an original crepe filled with fresh strawberries, green tea ice cream, and nutella. It was so good that sharing was hard. I wanted it all to myself!

Finding this place was a tad frustrating. It was nighttime so it was dark and hard to see the sign. We kept missing it! JFYI, it's located right next to Vidal Sassoon. Parking sucks too! BUT you can park at the Beverly Gardens. It's metered parking and free after 8PM.</Review>

< review>
Don't really understand what the hype is around Harajuku Crepes. Came here on a Saturday 15 minutes before closing and was amazed by how affordable these crepes are, and the option of choosing sesame and earl grey crepe batter. But after asking the cashier, I decided to stick with the original batter, since it was most popular. Included in the crepe, I had banana, sheet of mochi, nutella, and almonds (they ran out of whipped cream). The crepe itself was $3, and the toppings ranged form $0.25 - $1. Mine came out to be $6-7.

When I received my crepe, I noticed how small it was and how little toppings it came with... No wonder why it was so cheap! Secondly, just from holding the crepe, I already knew it wouldn't be good (or as good as other crepes I've had), because it wasn't the crispy crepe. It was really soft, like a pancake, which I'm not really a fan of.

It wasn't a "bad" crepe per se, but just not my cup of tea. I probably wouldn't come back...< /review>

< review>
I came here with a group of 9 on a Friday night. I got a matcha crepe with vanilla ice cream, whipped cream, and mochi. It came out to be $6. The crepe was rather smaller than other places, but still pretty good. The mochi was wrapped within the edges of the crepe, allowing me to eat ice cream and mochi in every bite.

One downside is that the place is rather small, so there wasn't much seating and we ended up standing outside to eat the crepes. In addition, waiting for the crepes took a while, especially considering the size of the crepes and the lack of customers while we were there.

Parking is also hard to find. Had to park near a park a block away.

Overall, not a bad crepe place, but definitely have had better with faster service.

Note: There is a minimum credit card charge of $6.<//review>

< Text>
Harajuku Crepe is a fantastic place to take a break from all the Rodeo Drive window shopping ;) Crepes here are A-MA-ZING!

The owner developed his skills at a creperie in Japan, and invented his own recipe for this venture. The not-so-secret ingredient that makes the crepes here extra special is MOCHI powder! It makes the crepe itself slightly thicker than French style crepes while still maintaining the fluffy softness we looove.

What's also great is the selection of flavors--original, green tea, earl grey and buckwheat (yes, buckwheat!)--ensures that you're never going to get bored of the menu. Since they're very generous with their toppings, the finished crepes are often monstrous.

Finally, a worthy successor to the now defunct crepe nazi on Sawtelle!< /Text>

< review>
My rating here would probably be 3.5 stars. I went bc I was visiting socal on a vacation, and I had read good reviews about this African American eatery that I wanted to support.
I ordered takeout, just their oxtail tacos to go, as that sounded great to me as a snack. I paid w/ credit card, which I don't recommend as they add a $1 cc charge. I would've paid by cash if I'd known. My total bill, with tip, was a bit pricey at ~$19. However, while I was waiting I asked if I could use their restroom, and they were very accommodating in letting me in, which I really appreciated.
Brought the food home to eat, and it was good. My only gripe was the cc charge, and not knowing about it before I used my cc.<//review>

< review>
Hard to notice from the street, as they have no sign up. But what my party had we all agreed was well done. The oxtail tacos were not too spicy, or too fatty. The seafood gumbo was well done, modest portion sizing. The BLT with green tomatoes (and fake bacon) was great - the remoulade was a highlight, and the tomatoes it overcooked nor too firm. The gries (grits fries) were a pleasant surprise, holding up in consistency and texture. Lastly, dessert was good takes on originals... Vegan pineapple upside-down cake, sweet potato pie with pecans, both delicious and not overly sweet. The peach cobbler on the other hand, was almost too syrupy. Overall, a new favorite.<//review>

<Review>This is a hidden gem in Los Angeles, my personal favorites for take out are the turkey sandwich, Oxtail street tacos, and THE SHRIMP AND GRITS.
My first visit here was on a Weds afternoon, my girlfriend say come on let's to this place on Pico. I had no idea where we were going, much to my surprise it was My Two Cents.
It is a very small quaint place(maybe 16 sets), I knew once inside with the aromas in the air that this was going to be a great treat. I enjoyed everything that day and took some home to my hubby, I now drop in for take out often.
I can't believe the Culinary Delights that come from their small kitchen.
I was told that the owner was a lady chef and that she no longer did all the cooking, however I was not disappointed.
They offer seafood, Cajun foods, Oxtail tacos, salads, gumbo, veggie options, as well an assortment of desserts
I would call My Two Cents an American restaurant with a twist of  Southern cooking.
The food here is consistent, fresh, tasty, the potions are regular size.Customer service is excellent!
This small place delivers a lot, LOVE, LOVE, LOVE this place.
The restroom is clean, there is street parking, they accept all major credit cards and is visible from the street. Look for the Fork, Spoon and Heart symbol it will help you find it easier. There is a strip mall on the corner going west and it is on the north side of the street.
TREAT YO SELF!<//Review><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x80c2b9102499c36b:0x82756ea2fe8a506e</Gmap_id></record>

<pictures>None< /pictures>< Review>
I really like this place actually!  The staff are very friendly.  The ambiance is cool too.  And the thing that matters - the food?  It's actually very good.  I got the fried chicken and it's really tasty.  It's boneless and the breading is very well done.  I also got the greens and the sweet potato cobbler as the sides.  Both were very good too, but if you don't like coconut, you won't like the cobbler.  I do so I loved it.  My friend hates coconut and she bailed out fast.

I also got the Halloween cake which was huge and tasty.  The frosting got a little intense though (very sweet) but that's how some people love their frosting.

I'm docking it one star only cuz the cost is a tad bit high, and some of the dishes take a little long to come out.  But for the dish time... that means they're making your order fresh so that's a good thing too!

It's a great place to try out if you're feeling like some soul food.< /Review>

<Review>This place is on point.  Food is very good and it's nice to see healthy versions of traditional soul food dishes. They do not drown their food in salt yet everything is flavorful.  Standouts for me include the bbq chicken, the pork chop, the sweet potato crumble side and the gumbo. They use a vegan andouille sausage in their gumbo that I can't believe is actually vegan.  So good!  The homemade desserts are delicious and there is a nice assortment.  Also, if they put out out a freshly baked cake of any flavor, they put the slices from the previous cake on sale for $3!  So you know that their baked goods are truly fresh.  The place is on the small side and the tables are often full but this is to be expected given their popularity. Also buy a lottery ticket if you are able to park in their lot because you are clearly lucky.  In fact, go in the afternoon on a weekend when the traffic is a little lighter. I highly recommend!</Review>< name>
GLW< /name>

<rate>5</rate>< Text>
If any restaurant can be personified with the human characteristics "friendly," "charismatic," or, more generally be said to "have personality," it would be My Two Cents. My Two Cents is that cheerful friend who's always glad to see you, never boring, never down. Go there if YOU are (down) and see if you can possibly stay that way.
The owner, the staff, everyone is great. And the food? Great.
Try the oxtail tacos, the stuffed pork chop. The biscuits. The corn bread (which is the best this southerner has ever had, bar none).
Downsides? It's popular, and the seating system is Darwinian and could use some more organization on nights too chilly for the outdoor seating to kick in. Oh, and no alcohol, but you can bring it in.<//Text>

< Text>
The food was delicious!!! I came with a group of five and we all ordered the shrimp and grits. We all agreed that the food was yummy. However, we ordered the biscuits and honey and was taken aback. The biscuit tasted more like a scone. It even had a lemon flavor to it.

Though it was still pretty good, it was not what we were expecting. The place is small and almost fastfood like. You order at the counter and find a place to sit. But, all in all, it was good - just not a place you would want to take your date for dinner<//Text>

< Review>
I want to love this place, but sadly, it's just OK. The customer service was excellent =5stars, the staff is friendly and very helpful. They share a small parking lot, so parking can be a challenge.

Now on to the food. I ordered take-out. Maybe that is the first mistake on my part. It is very rare to have food taste as good at home when it has been stuffed in a box. I ordered the oxtail tacos, which I admit were very tasty, but for $9 for 3 small tacos? Not worth the drive. I also ordered the sweet potato pie and the peach cobbler. I THREW away the $6 cobbler that was no more than 3oz. It was awful. The dough was gummy and the peaches tasted like pumpkin spice and something else that was just off. I can eat almost anything, but that cobbler was terrible. The sweet potato pie was average at best and for $8.50, definitely not worth it.

Sorry , I won't be back, at least for desserts or take out.<//Review>

Hrllo my name is Vickie W. And My parents and I yravelef from Phoenix, Az to be on the Price is Right.  Well after the taping of the show we decided on soul food.  Man oh Man,  first of all the name of the restaurant will make you wonder.  So , I asked why the name "My 2 cents(cents symbol).... She said, " because its my money and my opinion".  Unique...huh?  Then when  you walk in the concierge addresses you as "family", he also explained the ingredients for our meals, the menu,  the favorites, even right down to waythe meat is processed and prepared.  The little nook and cranny of a place is clean,  and authentic with touches of granny's tin can cups that was filled with ice for the fresh mint water. The chef and waiters are friendly, the food and deserts are fresh and delicious.  Just a note, when you visit tell 'em its your first time .  God bless 2cents.< /Text>

<pics>None<//pics><review>The most incredible gluten-free food ever so happy to be here!< /review></record></dataset><record>
<userid>108629487273276198215< /userid><user_name>Dan Gordon< /user_name><date>1527304257661</date><rating>5<//rating>< review>
One of the BEST MEALS of my life. I had so many foodgasms here that I felt inappropriate eating this food in public. The food is so good that my friend and I ordered a second dinner. And three desserts.

I feel like we just walked out of Willy Wonka's Chocolate Factory. The vibe in here is lively, fun, and so warm and welcoming. It's like a neighborhood block party that's been waiting for you.

Grit Fries. If the Burger King French Toast Sticks has a love child with Mozzarella Sticks on top of cornbread, it'd be these grit fries. A touch sweet. And so delicious it made me angry because I can't understand how someone could make something this different and stupid good.

Sweet Potato Crumble. This little side with pecans and I don't know what (wizard magic??) took me back to my childhood. But even the food then wasn't this good.

Kobe Burger. This was our second dinner. WORTH IT. It's a special. So if it's not here when you come, I'm jealous of what's there that I'm missing out on. Everything is great here.

BBQ Fried Chicken. Crispy. Meaty. Savory. The first bite emptied out all the thoughts in my brain. I felt dumb.

Seafood Gumbo. A bowl of Soul food that warmed my soul. So much fresh crab, scallops, crab legs. It's wonderful.

Sweet Potato Pound Cake. If you're vegan, you can eat this. If you're not vegan, you wouldn't know it is. Not-too-sweet. Moist. Incredible.

Chocolate Bread Pudding. After I took my first bite, my buddy and I Iocked eyes. I'm not gay but my heart was so filled with joy and love that if I had a ring in my pocket, I would've proposed to him. #loveislove #eatdessertwithyourlover

Peach Cobbler. Again, not too sweet. So delicious. I'm running out of words because the foodgasms have left me speechless and dumb.

Still reading?!? Wow. Ok. Look...

So many choices on where to eat, right?!? It's like trying to pick what to watch on Netflix. I GET IT. Let it go, Indiana. Let it go. Come here. Have fun. Move on with your life decisions.<//review>

< review>
an interesting take on soul food. it seems like a healthy fusion southern restaurant.  we had the fried catfish with black eye pea stew. grilled catfish with red beans and quinoa.  also a a fried green tomato po boy sandwich with greens.

everything fell short of expectations but was not bad. I simply don't like this style of healthy southern.   the red beans were tiny red beans and were overwhelmed by the quinoa. didn't even come close to traditional red beans

the catfish was cooked good. however the remoulade tasted more like homemade bbq sauce. not bad but not good either.   the fried green tomato had a good sauce but the tomato I feel was cut too thick and they weren't tender.

the staff was very nice. the place is small and I feel for this style of food it should be located about 1 mile north. the area it is in is a little shady.<//review>

<Review>This place has energy, love, and good ass food. An unassuming small cafe with elevated taste inspired by southern comfort food. Perfectly cooked shrimp atop creamy parmesan grits topped off with a french broth. Perfectly fried (but not heavy) boneless breast drizzled with bbq sauce, leafy greens cooked and seasoned just enough to have that stewed flavor but not cooked to death as they so often are. Fried catfish with mashed potatoes and fried brussel sprouts (yes, I know...your mouth is watering). The Chef has a presence and interacts with customers. She is down to earth, lively, and passionate about her craft. The only downfall was that the service was a little off. The waiter kept forgetting to bring us items and we had to remind him a couple of times. It was the end of the day so I tried to blame it on exhaustion :-).</Review>< Pics>

< Text>
So I went for the first time with my mom and the food was interestingly different and very good. It's definitely not the usual fast food soul food place we're used to. I had a healthier but tasty fried chicken, braised greens (greens with no meat); my mom had the popular shrimp with corn grits and again it was really tasty! Strange but tasty lol lol The plates are cute and kinda of bamboo looking..The service was great, they were friendly and helpful when deciding what to eat. The girl at the front was adorable and lovely as was the owner and that's a great sign to me!  A few things for me to remember about this day besides lunch with my wonderful mom was Meagan Good was there having lunch with her husband so no one bothered them AND the owner had the tree in front cut into the shape of a heart ! That was cool! Soooo- don't go with "soul food" expectations; just show up hungry! The desserts are to die for .....sweet potato cake and peach cobbler!!!!!!!!</Text>

Have dedicated table bussers/resetters.
